{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01AKVykGEgXYuDaGyxsXW3yg","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01MdciCXMgheYphSwCTdmRHw","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/numpy/lib/_rolling_median.py","content":"\"\"\"\nRolling median function for NumPy.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport functools\nimport numpy as np\nfrom numpy._core import overrides\nfrom numpy._utils import set_module\n\n\narray_function_dispatch = functools.partial(\n    overrides.array_function_dispatch, module='numpy')\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_dispatcher(a, window_size, axis=None, mode=None):\n    \"\"\"Dispatcher for rolling_median.\"\"\"\n    return (a,)\n\n\n@array_function_dispatch(_rolling_median_dispatcher)\n@set_module('numpy')\ndef rolling_median(a, window_size, *, axis=-1, mode='valid'):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute a rolling median along a given axis.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    a : array_like\n        Input array or object that can be converted to an array.\n    window_size : int\n        Size of the rolling window. Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which the rolling median is computed. Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output size:\n\n        - 'valid': Only compute where the window fully overlaps (default).\n          Output size: max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n        - 'same': Output same size as input. Window centered when possible.\n          Output size: n\n        - 'full': Compute for all possible window positions, including partial overlaps.\n          Output size: n + window_size - 1\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    output : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians. The shape depends on the input array and mode.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If window_size is not a positive integer or mode is invalid.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median of an array.\n    numpy.convolve : Discrete convolution with similar mode parameter.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window across the array\n    and computing the median of values within each window position.\n\n    For 1-D arrays, the window slides along the specified axis. The median\n    is computed using `numpy.partition` for efficiency.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3, mode='same')\n    array([1., 2., 3., 4., 5.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3, mode='full')\n    array([1., 1.5, 2., 3., 4., 5., 5.])\n    \"\"\"\n    # Input validation\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(f\"window_size must be an integer, got {type(window_size)}\")\n\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n    if window_size <= 0:\n        raise ValueError(f\"window_size must be positive, got {window_size}\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got '{mode}'\")\n\n    # Handle 1-D case\n    if a.ndim == 0:\n        raise ValueError(\"rolling_median requires an array of at least 1 dimension\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if a.ndim == 1:\n        # For 1-D arrays, ignore the axis parameter\n        return _rolling_median_1d(a, window_size, mode)\n    else:\n        # For multi-dimensional arrays, apply along the specified axis\n        axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\n        return _rolling_median_nd(a, window_size, axis, mode)\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_1d(a, window_size, mode):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 1-D array.\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n\n    # Handle edge case where window is larger than array\n    if window_size > n:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return np.array([], dtype=a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            # Return array of NaNs for all elements\n            result = np.empty(n, dtype=np.float64)\n            result[:] = np.nan\n            return result\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Pad the array and compute\n            padded = np.pad(a, (window_size - 1, 0), mode='edge')\n            return _compute_rolling_median_valid(padded, window_size)\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_valid(a, window_size)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_same(a, window_size)\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_full(a, window_size)\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_valid(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'valid' mode (output size: n - window_size + 1).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    out_size = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n\n    if out_size == 0:\n        return np.array([], dtype=np.float64)\n\n    result = np.empty(out_size, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        window = a[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_same(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'same' mode (output size: n, same as input).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    result = np.empty(n, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Calculate padding needed to keep output same size\n    # For odd window_size, center the window\n    # For even window_size, bias toward the left\n    left_pad = (window_size - 1) // 2\n    right_pad = window_size - 1 - left_pad\n\n    # Pad the input array\n    padded = np.pad(a, (left_pad, right_pad), mode='edge')\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    for i in range(n):\n        window = padded[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_full(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'full' mode (output size: n + window_size - 1).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    out_size = n + window_size - 1\n    result = np.empty(out_size, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Pad the input array with edge values\n    padded = np.pad(a, (window_size - 1, 0), mode='edge')\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        window = padded[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_nd(a, window_size, axis, mode):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for n-dimensional array along a specific axis.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Move the axis to the last position for easier computation\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, -1)\n    original_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n    # Reshape to 2-D (rest of dimensions, last dimension)\n    a_2d = a_moved.reshape(-1, a_moved.shape[-1])\n\n    # Compute rolling median for each row\n    n = a_2d.shape[-1]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        out_size = n\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        out_size = n + window_size - 1\n\n    result_2d = np.empty((a_2d.shape[0], out_size), dtype=np.float64)\n\n    for i in range(a_2d.shape[0]):\n        result_2d[i, :] = _rolling_median_1d(a_2d[i, :], window_size, mode)\n\n    # Reshape back to original shape (with modified last dimension)\n    new_shape = list(original_shape[:-1]) + [out_size]\n    result = result_2d.reshape(new_shape)\n\n    # Move the axis back to original position\n    result = np.moveaxis(result, -1, axis)\n\n    return result\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":225,"cache_read_input_tokens":61443,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":225},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"00ccd3e7-64c9-4c60-a056-9ca0b3968b3a","uuid":"7d5b5174-b902-40c4-ac0a-dd8ccb433293"}

Calculate padding needed to keep output same size\n    # For odd window_size, center the window\n    # For even window_size, bias toward the left\n    left_pad = (window_size - 1) // 2\n    right_pad = window_size - 1 - left_pad\n\n    # Pad the input array with edge values\n    padded = np.pad(a, (window_size - 1, 0), mode='edge')\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        window = padded[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_nd(a, window_size, axis, mode):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for n-dimensional array along a specific axis.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Move the axis to the last position for easier computation\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, -1)\n    original_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n    # Reshape to 2-D (rest of dimensions, last dimension)\n    a_2d = a_moved.reshape(-1, a_moved.shape[-1])\n\n    # Compute rolling median for each row\n    n = a_2d.shape[-1]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        out_size = n\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        out_size = n + window_size - 1\n\n    result_2d = np.empty((a_2d.shape[0], out_size), dtype=np.float64)\n\n    for i in range(a_2d.shape[0]):\n        result_2d[i, :] = _rolling_median_1d(a_2d[i, :], window_size, mode)\n\n    # Reshape back to original shape (with modified last dimension)\n    new_shape = list(original_shape[:-1]) + [out_size]\n    result = result_2d.reshape(new_shape)\n\n    # Move the axis back to original position\n    result = np.moveaxis(result, -1, axis)\n\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

The shape depends on the input array and mode.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If window_size is not a positive integer or mode is invalid.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median of an array.\n    numpy.convolve : Discrete convolution with similar mode parameter.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window across the array\n    and computing the median of values within each window position.\n\n    For 1-D arrays, the window slides along the specified axis. The median\n    is computed using `numpy.partition` for efficiency.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3, mode='same')\n    array([1., 2., 3., 4., 5.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3, mode='full')\n    array([1., 1.5, 2., 3., 4., 5., 5.])\n    \"\"\"\n    # Handle edge case where window is larger than array\n    if window_size > n:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return np.array([], dtype=a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            # Return array of NaNs for all elements\n            result = np.empty(n, dtype=np.float64)\n            result[:] = np.nan\n            return result\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Pad the array and compute\n            padded = np.pad(a, (window_size - 1, 0), mode='edge')\n            return _compute_rolling_median_valid(padded, window_size)\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_valid(a, window_size)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_same(a, window_size)\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_full(a, window_size)\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_valid(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'valid' mode (output size: n - window_size + 1).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    out_size = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n\n    if out_size == 0:\n        return np.array([], dtype=np.float64)\n\n    result = np.empty(out_size, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        window = a[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_same(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'same' mode (output size: n, same as input).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    result = np.empty(n, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Calculate padding needed to keep output same size\n    # For odd window_size, center the window\n    # For even window_size, bias toward the left\n    left_pad = (window_size - 1) // 2\n    right_pad = window_size - 1 - left_pad\n\n    # Pad the input array\n    padded = np.pad(a, (left_pad, right_pad), mode='edge')\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    for i in range(n):\n        window = padded[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_full(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'full' mode (output size: n + window_size - 1).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    out_size = n + window_size - 1\n    result = np.empty(out_size, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Pad the input array with edge values\n    padded = np.pad(a, (window_size - 1, 0), mode='edge')\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        window = padded[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_nd(a, window_size, axis, mode):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for n-dimensional array along a specific axis.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Move the axis to the last position for easier computation\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, -1)\n    original_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n    # Reshape to 2-D (rest of dimensions, last dimension)\n    a_2d = a_moved.reshape(-1, a_moved.shape[-1])\n\n    # Compute rolling median for each row\n    n = a_2d.shape[-1]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        out_size = n\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        out_size = n + window_size - 1\n\n    result_2d = np.empty((a_2d.shape[0], out_size), dtype=np.float64)\n\n    for i in range(a_2d.shape[0]):\n        result_2d[i, :] = _rolling_median_1d(a_2d[i, :], window_size, mode)\n\n    # Reshape back to original shape (with modified last dimension)\n    new_shape = list(original_shape[:-1]) + [out_size]\n    result = result_2d.reshape(new_shape)\n\n    # Move the axis back to original position\n    result = np.moveaxis(result, -1, axis)\n\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":8,"oldLines":6,"newStart":8,"newLines":9,"lines":[" from numpy._utils import set_module"," "," ","+__all__ = ['rolling_median']","+","+"," array_function_dispatch = functools.partial(","     overrides.array_function_dispatch, module='numpy')"," "]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

The median\n    is computed using `numpy.partition` for efficiency.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3, mode='same')\n    array([1., 2., 3., 4., 5.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, window_size=3, mode='full')\n    array([1., 1.5, 2., 3., 4., 5., 5.])\n    \"\"\"\n    # Input validation\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(f\"window_size must be an integer, got {type(window_size)}\")\n\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n    if window_size <= 0:\n        raise ValueError(f\"window_size must be positive, got {window_size}\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got '{mode}'\")\n\n    # Handle 1-D case\n    if a.ndim == 0:\n        raise ValueError(\"rolling_median requires an array of at least 1 dimension\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if a.ndim == 1:\n        # For 1-D arrays, ignore the axis parameter\n        return _rolling_median_1d(a, window_size, mode)\n    else:\n        # For multi-dimensional arrays, apply along the specified axis\n        axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\n        return _rolling_median_nd(a, window_size, axis, mode)\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_1d(a, window_size, mode):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 1-D array.\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_valid(a, window_size)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_same(a, window_size)\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        return _compute_rolling_median_full(a, window_size)\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_valid(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'valid' mode (output size: n - window_size + 1).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    out_size = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n\n    if out_size == 0:\n        return np.array([], dtype=np.float64)\n\n    result = np.empty(out_size, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        window = a[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_same(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'same' mode (output size: n, same as input).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    result = np.empty(n, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Calculate padding needed to keep output same size\n    # For odd window_size, center the window\n    # For even window_size, bias toward the left\n    left_pad = (window_size - 1) // 2\n    right_pad = window_size - 1 - left_pad\n\n    # Pad the input array\n    padded = np.pad(a, (left_pad, right_pad), mode='edge')\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    for i in range(n):\n        window = padded[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _compute_rolling_median_full(a, window_size):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for 'full' mode (output size: n + window_size - 1).\n    \"\"\"\n    n = len(a)\n    out_size = n + window_size - 1\n    result = np.empty(out_size, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Pad the input array with edge values\n    padded = np.pad(a, (window_size - 1, 0), mode='edge')\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    for i in range(out_size):\n        window = padded[i:i + window_size]\n        result[i] = np.median(window)\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_nd(a, window_size, axis, mode):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute rolling median for n-dimensional array along a specific axis.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Move the axis to the last position for easier computation\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, -1)\n    original_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n    # Reshape to 2-D (rest of dimensions, last dimension)\n    a_2d = a_moved.reshape(-1, a_moved.shape[-1])\n\n    # Compute rolling median for each row\n    n = a_2d.shape[-1]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        out_size = n\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        out_size = n + window_size - 1\n\n    result_2d = np.empty((a_2d.shape[0], out_size), dtype=np.float64)\n\n    for i in range(a_2d.shape[0]):\n        result_2d[i, :] = _rolling_median_1d(a_2d[i, :], window_size, mode)\n\n    # Reshape back to original shape (with modified last dimension)\n    new_shape = list(original_shape[:-1]) + [out_size]\n    result = result_2d.reshape(new_shape)\n\n    # Move the axis back to original position\n    result = np.moveaxis(result, -1, axis)\n\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":172,"oldLines":8,"newStart":172,"newLines":8,"lines":["     out_size = n + window_size -
